    (function () {
        if ( typeof window.CustomEvent === "function" ) return false;
        function CustomEvent ( event, params ) {
            params = params || { bubbles: false, cancelable: false, detail: null };
            var evt = document.createEvent( 'CustomEvent' );
            evt.initCustomEvent( event, params.bubbles, params.cancelable, params.detail );
            return evt;
        }

        CustomEvent.prototype = window.Event.prototype;

        window.CustomEvent = CustomEvent;
    })();
</script>

                    s.setAttribute('data-test', script.test);

                        s.defer = 'defer';

                                loader.register(true);
                            }
                            if (d.readyState === 'interactive' || d.readyState === 'complete') {
                                loader.ready();
                            }
                        };

                        s.async = 'async';
                    }
                    s.src = script.src;
                    return s;

    <script type="application/ld+json">{"mainEntity":{"headline":"Architectural design of anode materials for superior alkali-ion (Li/Na/K) batteries storage","description":"Developing high-performance anode materials remains a significant challenge for clean energy storage systems. Herein, we investigated the (MXene/MoSe2@C) heterostructure hybrid nanostructure as a superior anode material for application in lithium, sodium, and potassium ion batteries (LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs). Moreover, the anode structure’s stability was examined via the open-source Large-scale atomic/molecular massively Parallel Simulator code. Our results indicated that the migration of SIBs toward the anode material is significantly greater than other ions during charge and discharge cycles. Therefore, SIBs systems can be competitive with PIBs and LIBs systems. In addition, the average values of the potential energies for the anode materials/ions complexes are about ~ − 713.65, ~  − 2030.41, and ~ − 912.36 kcal mol−1 in systems LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs, respectively. This study provides a rational design strategy to develop high-performance anode materials in SIBs/PIBs/LIBs systems, which can be developed for other transition metal chalcogenide-based composites as a superior anode of alkali metal ion battery storage     <meta name="dc.title" content="Architectural design of anode materials for superior alkali-ion (Li/Na/K) batteries storage">
    <meta name="dc.source" content="Scientific Reports 2024 14:1">
    <meta name="dc.format" content="text/html">
    <meta name="dc.publisher" content="Nature Publishing Group">
    <meta name="dc.date" content="2024-02-17">
    <meta name="dc.type" content="OriginalPaper">
    <meta name="dc.language" content="En">

    <meta name="dc.rightsAgent" content="journalpermissions@springernature.com">
    <meta name="dc.description" content="Developing high-performance anode materials remains a significant challenge for clean energy storage systems. Herein, we investigated the (MXene/MoSe2@C) heterostructure hybrid nanostructure as a superior anode material for application in lithium, sodium, and potassium ion batteries (LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs). Moreover, the anode structure’s stability was examined via the open-source Large-scale atomic/molecular massively Parallel Simulator code. Our results indicated that the migration of SIBs toward the anode material is significantly greater than other ions during charge and discharge cycles. Therefore, SIBs systems can be competitive with PIBs and LIBs systems. In addition, the average values of the potential energies for the anode materials/ions complexes are about ~ − 713.65, ~  − 2030.41, and ~ − 912.36&amp;nbsp;kcal&amp;nbsp;mol−1 in systems LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs, respectively. This study provides a rational design strategy to develop high-performance anode materials in SIBs/PIBs/LIBs systems, which can be developed for other transition metal chalcogenide-based composites as a superior anode of alkali metal ion battery storage systems.">

    <meta name="description" content="Developing high-performance anode materials remains a significant challenge for clean energy storage systems. Herein, we investigated the (MXene/MoSe2@C) heterostructure hybrid nanostructure as a superior anode material for application in lithium, sodium, and potassium ion batteries (LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs). Moreover, the anode structure’s stability was examined via the open-source Large-scale atomic/molecular massively Parallel Simulator code. Our results indicated that the migration of SIBs toward the anode material is significantly greater than other ions during charge and discharge cycles. Therefore, SIBs systems can be competitive with PIBs and LIBs systems. In addition, the average values of the potential energies for the anode materials/ions complexes are about ~ − 713.65, ~  − 2030.41, and ~ − 912.36&amp;nbsp;kcal&amp;nbsp;mol−1 in systems LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs, respectively. This study provides a rational design strategy to develop high-performance anode materials in SIBs/PIBs/LIBs systems, which can be developed for other transition metal chalcogenide-based composites as a superior anode of alkali metal ion battery storage systems.">

                    <h1 class="c-article-title" data-test="article-title" data-article-title="">Architectural design of anode materials for superior alkali-ion (Li/Na/K) batteries storage</h1>
                    <ul class="c-article-author-list c-article-author-list--short js-no-scroll" data-test="authors-list" data-component-authors-activator="authors-list"><li class="c-article-author-list__item"><a data-test="author-name" data-track="click" data-track-action="open author" data-track-label="link" href="#auth-Afsaneh-Ghahari-Aff1" data-author-popup="auth-Afsaneh-Ghahari-Aff1" data-author-search="Ghahari, Afsaneh" data-track-context="researcher popup with no profile" data-track-index="1_2">Afsaneh Ghahari</a><sup class="u-js-hide"><a href="#Aff1" tabindex="-1">1</a></sup> &amp; </li><li class="c-article-author-list__item"><a data-test="author-name" data-track="click" data-track-action="open author" data-track-label="link" href="#auth-Heidar-Raissi-Aff1" data-author-popup="auth-Heidar-Raissi-Aff1" data-author-search="Raissi, Heidar" data-corresp-id="c1" data-track-context="researcher popup with no profile" data-track-index="2_2">Heidar Raissi<svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-mail-medium"></use></svg></a><sup class="u-js-hide"><a href="#Aff1" tabindex="-1">1</a></sup>&nbsp;</li></ul>

                    

                    <p class="c-article-info-details" data-container-section="info">
                        
    <a data-test="journal-link" href="/srep" data-track="click" data-track-action="journal homepage" data-track-category="article body" data-track-label="link"><i data-test="journal-title">Scientific Reports</i></a>

                        <b data-test="journal-volume"><span class="u-visually-hidden">volume</span>&nbsp;14</b>, Article&nbsp;number:&nbsp;<span data-test="article-number">3959</span> (<span data-test="article-publication-year">2024</span>)
            <a href="#citeas" class="c-article-info-details__cite-as u-hide-print" data-track="click" data-track-action="cite this article" data-track-label="link">Cite this article</a>
                    </p>

        <div class="c-article-body">
            <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>Developing high-performance anode materials remains a significant challenge for clean energy storage systems. Herein, we investigated the (MXene/MoSe<sub>2</sub>@C) heterostructure hybrid nanostructure as a superior anode material for application in lithium, sodium, and potassium ion batteries (LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs). Moreover, the anode structure’s stability was examined via the open-source Large-scale atomic/molecular massively Parallel Simulator code. Our results indicated that the migration of SIBs toward the anode material is significantly greater than other ions during charge and discharge cycles. Therefore, SIBs systems can be competitive with PIBs and LIBs systems. In addition, the average values of the potential energies for the anode materials/ions complexes are about ~ − 713.65, ~  − 2030.41, and ~ − 912.36&nbsp;kcal&nbsp;mol<sup>−1</sup> in systems LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs, respectively. This study provides a rational design strategy to develop high-performance anode materials in SIBs/PIBs/LIBs systems, which can be developed for other transition metal chalcogenide-based composites as a superior anode of alkali metal ion battery storage systems.</p></div></div></section>

                        <section data-title="Introduction"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Introduction</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>The development of sustainable and clean energy sources is one of the most pressing issues in today’s society as an alternative to fossil fuel technologies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Sharma, R. &amp; Kumari, A. Potential applications of biorenewable nanocomposite materials for electrocatalysis, energy storage, and wastewater treatment. In Biorenewable Nanocomposite Materials, Vol. 1: Electrocatalysts and Energy Storage 25–46 (ACS Publications, 2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e400">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Poizot, P. et al. Opportunities and challenges for organic electrodes in electrochemical energy storage. Chem. Rev. 20, 6490–6557 (2020)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e403">2</a></sup>. Notwithstanding these advances, rechargeable battery emerges as the optimal choice for an energy storage system due to their minimal maintenance needs, high efficiency, and extended cycle life in energy conversion<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Cheng, F. et al. Functional materials for rechargeable batteries. Adv. Mater. 23, 1695–1715 (2011)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e407">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Zhu, Z. et al. Rechargeable batteries for grid scale energy storage. Chem. Rev. 122, 16610–16751 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e410">4</a></sup>. In the construction of a smart-grid energy storage system (ESS), the development of secondary batteries necessitates larger quantities of materials<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Zhang, Z. et al. A review of technologies and applications on versatile energy storage systems. Renew. Sustain. Energy Rev. 148, 111263 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e414">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Mohan, I. et al. Potential of potassium and sodium-ion batteries as the future of energy storage: Recent progress in anodic materials. J. Energy Storage 55, 105625 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e417">6</a></sup>. As a result, striking a delicate balance among crucial factors, such as power density, life, energy density, safety, and cost, becomes imperative for these secondary batteries<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Griffiths, G. Review of developments in lithium secondary battery technology. Underw. Technol. 33, 153–163 (2016)." href="#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e421">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Liu, Q. et al. Low cost and superior safety industrial grade lithium dual-ion batteries with a second life. Energy Technol. 6(10), 1994–2000 (2018)." href="#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e421_1">8</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Dehghani-Sanij, A. R. et al. Study of energy storage systems and environmental challenges of batteries. Renew. Sustain. Energy Rev. 104, 192–208 (2019)." href="#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e421_2">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Braun, P. V. et al. High power rechargeable batteries. Curr. Opin. Solid State Mater. Sci. 16, 186–198 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e424">10</a></sup>. Alkali metal ion batteries, such as lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), and potassium-ion batteries (PIBs), are essential rechargeable battery technologies that are essential for renewable energy applications<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Mohan, I. et al. Potential of potassium and sodium-ion batteries as the future of energy storage: Recent progress in anodic materials. J. Energy Storage 55, 105625 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e428">6</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yang, L. et al. Design of black phosphorous derivatives with excellent stability and ion-kinetics for alkali metal-ion battery. Energy Storage Mater. 35, 283–309 (2021)." href="#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e431">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Xu, Z.-L. et al. Graphitic carbon materials for advanced sodium-ion batteries. Small Methods 3, 1800227 (2019)." href="#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e431_1">12</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Gong, Y. et al. Metal selenides anode materials for sodium ion batteries: Synthesis, modification, and application. Small 19, 2206194 (2023)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e434">13</a></sup>. For instance, the LIBs rechargeable battery has dominated the electric vehicles and portable electronics market over the past two decades<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yang, Z. et al. Sustainable electric vehicle batteries for a sustainable world: Perspectives on battery cathodes, environment, supply chain, manufacturing, life cycle, and policy. Adv. Energy Mater. 12, 2200383 (2022)." href="#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e439">14</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Eftekhari, A. Lithium batteries for electric vehicles: From economy to research strategy (2019)." href="#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e439_1">15</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Desaulty, A.-M. et al. Tracing the origin of lithium in Li-ion batteries using lithium isotopes. Nat. Commun. 13, 4172 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e442">16</a></sup>. However, the uneven distribution and insufficient Lithium resources raised some serious concerns about the future deployment of LIBs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Xu, P. et al. A materials perspective on direct recycling of lithium-ion batteries: Principles, challenges and opportunities. Adv. Funct. Mater. 33, 2213168 (2023)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e446">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Tian, Y. et al. Promises and challenges of next-generation “beyond Li-ion” batteries for electric vehicles and grid decarbonization. Chem. Rev. 121, 1623–1669 (2020)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e449">18</a></sup>. Over the last few decades, there has been significant progress in exploring battery alternatives beyond LIBs. Among these, sodium and potassium-ion batteries (SIBs/PIBs) are gaining increasing attention due to their promising potential. Next-generation batteries based on Na<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup>, alkali ions common in the earth’s crust, are considered promising alternatives in future energy storage due to their abundance, high energy density and low cost<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Song, K. et al. Recent progress on the alloy-based anode for sodium-ion batteries and potassium-ion batteries. Small 174, 1903194 (2021)." href="#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e457">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Du, P. et al. Recent progress on heterostructure materials for next-generation sodium/potassium ion batteries. Renew. Sustain. Energy Rev. 151, 111640 (2021)." href="#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e457_1">20</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Kumar, M. R. et al. Next generation 2D materials for anodes in battery applications. J. Power Sources 556, 232256 (2023)." href="#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e457_2">21</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Hao, H. et al. Review of multifunctional separators: Stabilizing the cathode and the anode for alkali (Li, Na, and K) metal–sulfur and selenium batteries. Chem. Rev. 122, 8053–8125 (2022)." href="#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e457_3">22</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Huang, Z.-X. et al. Advanced layered oxide cathodes for sodium/potassium-ion batteries: Development, challenges and prospects. Chem. Eng. J. 452, 139438 (2022)." href="#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e457_4">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Yuan, D. et al. Atomically thin materials for next-generation rechargeable batteries. Chem. Rev. 122, 957–999 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e460">24</a></sup>. Meanwhile, non-aqueous SIBs and PIBs have also been developed during the last decades, inspired by the lack of Li<sup>+</sup> resources<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Wang, J. et al. Prussian blue analogs (PBA) derived porous bimetal (Mn, Fe) selenide with carbon nanotubes as anode materials for sodium and potassium ion batteries. Chem. Eng. J. 382, 123050 (2020)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e467">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Xu, L. et al. V3Se4 embedded within N/P co-doped carbon fibers for sodium/potassium ion batteries. Chem. Eng. J. 419, 129607 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e470">26</a></sup>. Whereas compared with that of Li<sup>+</sup> (0.76&nbsp;Å, and molar mass 6.94&nbsp;g&nbsp;mol<sup>−1</sup>), the larger ionic radius (Na<sup>+</sup> = 1.02&nbsp;Å, and K<sup>+</sup> = 1.38&nbsp;Å) and the heavier atomic weights (Na<sup>+</sup> = 22.99&nbsp;g&nbsp;mol<sup>−1</sup>, K<sup>+</sup> = 39.10&nbsp;g&nbsp;mol<sup>−1</sup>) of Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup> lead to lots of trouble including higher diffusion barriers<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhao, Z. et al. Defective Bi2S3 anchored on CuS/C as an ultrafast and long-life anode for sodium-ion storage. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 15(3), 4011–4020 (2023)." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e495">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Liu, X. &amp; Ye, Z. Nitroaromatics as high-energy organic cathode materials for rechargeable alkali-ion (Li+, Na+, and K+) batteries. Adv. Energy Mater. 11(4), 2003281 (2021)." href="#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e495_1">28</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Eom, K. et al. Crystalline chlorinated contorted hexabenzocoronene: A universal organic anode for advanced alkali-ion batteries. J. Mater. Chem. A 9(36), 20607–20614 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e498">29</a></sup>. On the other hand, the larger ionic radius causes sluggish kinetics<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Huang, Y. et al. Storage mechanism of alkali metal ions in the hard carbon anode: An electrochemical viewpoint. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 13(32), 38441–38449 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e503">30</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Rao, Y. et al. Heterostructured WS2/MoS2@ carbon hollow microspheres anchored on graphene for high-performance Li/Na storage. Chem. Eng. J. 443, 136080 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e506">31</a></sup>, large volume change during insertion/extraction processes within the existing electrode materials<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Liu, C. et al. Surface modification and in situ carbon intercalation of two-dimensional niobium carbide as promising electrode materials for potassium-ion batteries. Chem. Eng. J. 431, 133838 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e510">32</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Ge, H. et al. In situ growth of CoSe2 coated in porous carbon layers as anode for efficient sodium-ion batteries. Energy Technol. 9(3), 2001074 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e513">33</a></sup>, poor cycling stability<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Qin, T. et al. Mechanistic insights into the electrochemical Li/Na/K-ion storage for aqueous bismuth anode. Energy Storage Mater. 45, 33–39 (2022)." href="#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e517">34</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yuan, Z. et al. Composites of NiSe2@C hollow nanospheres wrapped with Ti3C2Tx MXene for synergistic enhanced sodium storage. Chem. Eng. J. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cej.2021.132394
                  
                 (2022)." href="#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e517_1">35</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Li, C. et al. Ultra-small few-layered MoSe2 nanosheets encapsulated in nitrogen-doped porous carbon nanofibers to create large heterointerfaces for enhanced potassium-ion storage. Appl. Surf. Sci. 601, 154196 (2022)." href="#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e517_2">36</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Sun, N. et al. MXene-bonded flexible hard carbon film as anode for stable Na/K-ion storage. Adv. Funct. Mater. 29, 1906282 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e520">37</a></sup>, and short cycle life<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Dou, M. et al. Simultaneous cation-anion regulation of sodium vanadium phosphate cathode materials for high-energy and cycle-stable sodium-ion batteries. J. Power Sources 560, 232709 (2023)." href="#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e524">38</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Sun, J. et al. Assembly of flower-like VS2/N-doped porous carbon with expanded (001) plane on rGO for superior Na-ion and K-ion storage. Nano Res. 15, 4108–4116 (2022)." href="#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e524_1">39</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Yadav, S. K. et al. 14 Chalcogenide-based2D. Energy Appl. 2D Nanomater (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e527">40</a></sup>. Hence, identifying an appropriate electrode material capable of hosting various alkali ions poses a significant challenge due to the expanding ionic radius and distinct interactions with the host electrodes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Wang, H. et al. Recent advances in conversion-type electrode materials for post lithium-ion batteries. ACS Mater. Lett. 3(7), 956–977 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e531">41</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Wang, X. et al. Tailored template engineering of MoSe2/N, P-doped carbon nanospheres with sandwiched carbon and few-layered MoSe2 shells for stable and high-rate storage of Na+/K+-ions. J. Mater. Chem. A 9(33), 17780–17789 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e534">42</a></sup>. Hence, it is urgent to design advanced electrode materials with robust structures that allow fast diffusivity and high reversibility of Na<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup>, realizing rate capability, high capacity and outstanding cycling stability<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang, H. et al. Recent advances in conversion-type electrode materials for post lithium-ion batteries. ACS Mater. Lett. 3(7), 956–977 (2021)." href="#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e543">41</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang, X. et al. Tailored template engineering of MoSe2/N, P-doped carbon nanospheres with sandwiched carbon and few-layered MoSe2 shells for stable and high-rate storage of Na+/K+-ions. J. Mater. Chem. A 9(33), 17780–17789 (2021)." href="#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e543_1">42</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Xu, Y.-S. et al. High-performance cathode materials for potassium-ion batteries: Structural design and electrochemical properties. Adv. Mater. 33(36), 2100409 (2021)." href="#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e543_2">43</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wu, C. et al. Continuous carbon channels enable full Na-ion accessibility for superior room-temperature Na–S batteries. Adv. Mater. 34(8), 2108363 (2022)." href="#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e543_3">44</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang, T. et al. J. 457, 141363 (2023)." href="#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e543_4">45</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yang, D. et al. Enhanced high-rate capability and long cycle stability of FeS@ NCG nanofibers for sodium-ion battery anodes. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 14(39), 44303–44316 (2022)." href="#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e543_5">46</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yao, T. et al. Enhancing pseudocapacitive behavior of MOF-derived TiO2-x@ Carbon nanocubes via Mo-doping for high-performance sodium-ion capacitors. Compos. Part B Eng. 253, 110557 (2023)." href="#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e543_6">47</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Li, Q. et al. Carbon-supported single-atom metal materials for robust Li/Na/K batteries: A mini review. Mater. Today Sustain. 22, 100355 (2023)." href="#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e543_7">48</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Yin, H. et al. Recent advances in electrospun metal chalcogenide anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries. ACS Appl. Energy Mater. 6(3), 1155–1175 (2023)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e546">49</a></sup>. Graphite is the most widely used commercial anode material for LIBs, owing to increased battery life, energy storage, and fast charging capability<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yin, H. et al. Recent advances in electrospun metal chalcogenide anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries. ACS Appl. Energy Mater. 6(3), 1155–1175 (2023)." href="#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e550">49</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Askaruly, K. et al. A facile synthesis of graphite-coated amorphous SiO2 from biosources as anode material for libs. Mater. Today Commun. 34, 105136 (2023)." href="#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e550_1">50</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Qiao, Y. et al. Recycling of graphite anode from spent lithium-ion batteries: Advances and perspectives. EcoMat 5(4), e12321 (2023)." href="#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e550_2">51</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Han, M. et al. Evaluation of cathode electrodes in lithium-ion battery: Pitfalls and the befitting counter electrode. Small 19, 2208018 (2023)." href="#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e550_3">52</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Guo, J. et al. Unravelling and quantifying the aging processes of commercial Li (Ni0.5Co0.2Mn0.3)O2/graphite lithium-ion batteries under constant current cycling. J. Mater. Chem. A 11(1), 41–52 (2023)." href="#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e550_4">53</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ren, J. et al. Porous Co 2 VO 4 nanodisk as a high-energy and fast-charging anode for lithium-ion batteries. Nano-micro Lett. 14, 1–14 (2022)." href="#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e550_5">54</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Weiss, M. et al. Fast charging of lithium-ion batteries: A review of materials aspects. Adv. Energy Mater. 11(33), 2101126 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e553">55</a></sup>, and it has attracted much attention from scientists. In addition, graphite is unsuitable for high-energy-density AMIBs due to its small spacing interlayer and does not provide meaningful capacity, particularly for SIBs/PIBs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Zhang, H. et al. A comparative overview of carbon anodes for nonaqueous alkali metal-ion batteries. J. Mater. Chem. A 9(48), 27140–27169 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e557">56</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Liu, M. et al. Advances in carbon materials for sodium and potassium storage. Adv. Funct. Mater. 32(31), 2203117 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e560">57</a></sup>. Meanwhile, SIBs exhibit chemical behaviors similar to LIBs; however, the substantial ionic radius of Na<sup>+</sup> (1.02&nbsp;Å) inevitably leads to significant volume expansion during charge/discharge processes. Consequently, SIBs frequently exhibit restricted capacity and cycling instability when compared to LIBs. Hence, the central focus for enhancing the electrochemical performance of SIBs lies in the advancement of electrode materials characterized by both high capacity and prolonged cycle life. The exploration of two-dimensional (2D) materials in rechargeable batteries has received great attention as promising anode materials owing to, the capability of higher charging rates and their high surface area by metal ions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Wang, B. et al. Dual-redox sites guarantee high-capacity sodium storage in two-dimension conjugated metal-organic frameworks. Adv. Funct. Mater. 32(22), 2112072 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e566">58</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Yu, F. et al. Design and synthesis of electrode materials with both battery-type and capacitive charge storage. Energy Storage Mater. 22, 235–255 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e569">59</a></sup>. Therefore, developing anode materials with excellent comprehensive electrochemical performance and low cost is crucial for the wide-scale practical application of SIBs/PIBs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Wang, F. et al. Ni0.6Fe0.4Se2/rGO heterogenous nanocubes anode for stable and efficient Na/K-Ion storage. Adv. Mater. Interfaces 9(35), 2201626 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e574">60</a></sup>. MXenes, also recognized as 2D transition metal carbides, are becoming increasingly promising for the storage of sodium ions. This is due to their outstanding metallic electronic conductivity, which can reach up to 9880&nbsp;S&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>, along with a low diffusion barrier for Na<sup>+</sup> falling within the range of 0.1–0.2&nbsp;eV<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Er, D. et al. Ti3C2 MXene as a high capacity electrode material for metal (Li, Na, K, Ca) ion batteries. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 6(14), 11173–11179 (2014)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e582">61</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Zhang, C. et al. Transparent, flexible, and conductive 2D titanium carbide (MXene) films with high volumetric capacitance. Adv. Mater. 29(36), 1702678 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e585">62</a></sup>.</p><p>In recent years, there has been a rapid increase in research interest in carbon anodes in SIBs and PIBs, driven by the comparable electrochemical advantages of metallic Na and K compared to Li. Additionally, the reserves of sodium and potassium metals are positioned 6th (constituting 2.36% by weight) and seventh (making up 2.09% by weight)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Li, J. et al. Metal selenides find plenty of space in architecting advanced sodium/potassium ion batteries. Small 20, 2305021 (2023)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e592">63</a></sup>, respectively. These resources far exceed those of Li, which comprises only 0.0017% in weight<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Li, J. et al. Metal selenides find plenty of space in architecting advanced sodium/potassium ion batteries. Small 20, 2305021 (2023)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e596">63</a></sup>. Up to date, metal chalcogenides, such as selenides, metal oxides, and sulfides, have been extensively studied as promising active electrode composites for SIBs and PIBs. These materials are favored for their abundance in the Earth’s crust and high specific capacity, making them attractive candidates for advancing battery technologies. Amongst various anode materials, metal selenides, known for their cost-effectiveness, resource abundance, and relatively stable electrochemical performance, have garnered increasing attention. Over the past years, have attracted much attention for interest in insertion-type anodes, including Ti-based and carbonaceous, for advanced AMIB due to their stable cycling performance. Regarding these materials, they frequently demonstrate relatively theoretical capacities, typically below 280&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Zhao et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Zhao, X. et al. MoSe2 nanosheets perpendicularly grown on graphene with Mo–C bonding for sodium-ion capacitors. Nano Energy 47, 224–234 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e602">64</a></sup> developed the creation of 2D MoSe<sub>2</sub>@graphene nanocomposites tailored for Na<sup>+</sup> capacitors, achieving an impressive energy density of 82&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> with a corresponding power density of 63&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>. Despite their potential, these electrodes frequently face significant challenges, including substantial changes in volume during processes governing cycling. This results in the collapse of the active material’s structure, which leads to rapid capacity deterioration. Therefore, creating electrode materials with robust structures for effective storage of Li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup> with high performance remains a significant challenge. Simultaneously, additional research is needed to explore multifunctional electrode materials that offer both high capacity and extended lifespans, addressing the challenges posed by the energy crisis. Additionally, MoSe<sub>2</sub> is recognized as an inherent semiconductor possessing a band gap of approximately 1.1&nbsp;eV, narrower than that of MoS<sub>2</sub> (around 1.7&nbsp;eV). This narrower band gap suggests higher electronic conductivity, a quality advantageous for achieving a high-rate capability. These characteristics collectively make MoSe<sub>2</sub> a promising candidate for the electrode anode material in SIBs. MoSe<sub>2</sub> electrodes face difficulties, such as instability and inherent low electronic conductivity. These issues lead to subpar rate performance and cycling stability in practical applications. Researchers have utilized different carbon materials to generate hybrids or nanocomposites incorporating MoSe<sub>2</sub> to enhance its anode material properties, addressing issues such as low electrical conductivity and structural stability<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Gong, Y. et al. Metal selenides anode materials for sodium ion batteries: Synthesis, modification, and application. Small 19, 2206194 (2023)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e632">13</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Tanwar, S. et al. Structural and electrochemical performance of carbon coated molybdenum selenide nanocomposite for supercapacitor applications. J. Energy Storage 45, 103797 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e635">65</a></sup>. Graphene’s exceptional characteristics, such as expansive surface area, high conductivity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Zhu, J. et al. Graphene and graphene-based materials for energy storage applications. Small 10(17), 3480–3498 (2014)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e640">66</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Lemine, A. S. et al. Graphene a promising electrode material for supercapacitors—A review. Int. J. Energy Res. 42(14), 4284–4300 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e643">67</a></sup>, flexibility, and compatibility with other molecules, endow it with unique potential for application in supercapacitors<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Park, H. et al. Flexible graphene electrode-based organic photovoltaics with record-high efficiency. Nano Lett. 14, 5148–5154 (2014)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e647">68</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Wen, L. et al. Carbon nanotubes and graphene for flexible electrochemical energy storage: From materials to devices. Adv. Mater. 28(22), 4306–4337 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e650">69</a></sup>. Graphite materials commonly employed in commercial LIBs face limitations in accommodating Na<sup>+</sup> insertion, resulting in insufficient capacity (below 35&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Luo, Y. et al. A conjugated plier-linked nano-spacing graphite network for sodium-ion battery. Energy Storage Mater. 39, 70–80 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e658">70</a></sup>. Consequently, there is a critical need to develop high-performance and versatile anode materials to overcome the challenges affecting not only LIBs but also SIBs and PIBs. The layered structure of graphene, along with its high potential, has led to the study of other layered inorganic materials, including layered transition metal dichalcogenides such as SnSe<sub>2</sub>, SnS<sub>2</sub>, MoSe<sub>2</sub>, MoS<sub>2</sub>, and WS<sub>2</sub><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Sun, N. et al. MXene-bonded flexible hard carbon film as anode for stable Na/K-ion storage. Adv. Funct. Mater. 29, 1906282 (2019)." href="#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e672">37</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Dou, M. et al. Simultaneous cation-anion regulation of sodium vanadium phosphate cathode materials for high-energy and cycle-stable sodium-ion batteries. J. Power Sources 560, 232709 (2023)." href="#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e672_1">38</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Sun, J. et al. Assembly of flower-like VS2/N-doped porous carbon with expanded (001) plane on rGO for superior Na-ion and K-ion storage. Nano Res. 15, 4108–4116 (2022)." href="#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e672_2">39</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yadav, S. K. et al. 14 Chalcogenide-based2D. Energy Appl. 2D Nanomater (2022)." href="#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e672_3">40</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Wang, H. et al. Recent advances in conversion-type electrode materials for post lithium-ion batteries. ACS Mater. Lett. 3(7), 956–977 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e675">41</a></sup>. Layered transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) characterized by the MX<sub>2</sub> formula (where M can be Mo, Ti, Nb, Hf, Zr, Sn, V, Ta, W, and X can be Te, S, Se) exhibit a morphology of graphite-like and demonstrate impressive performance. The X atoms form the outer layer in this structure, sandwiching the arrangement of metals in a hexagonally close-packed structure, represented as X–M–X. The M–X bond within each layer is covalent, while van der Waals forces govern the interaction between layers. This unique arrangement and morphology make TMDs ideal for energy conversion and storage applications, due to their distinct electronic, chemical, and physical properties<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Von Lim, Y. et al. Rhenium disulfide nanosheets/carbon composite as novel anodes for high-rate and long lifespan sodium-ion batteries. Nano Energy 61, 626–636 (2019)." href="#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e682">71</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Liu, X. et al. Design strategy for mxene and metal chalcogenides/oxides hybrids for energy storage and conversion. SSRN Electron. J. 
                  https://doi.org/10.2139/ssrn.3993047
                  
                 (2022)." href="#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e682_1">72</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Yousaf, M. et al. A 3D trilayered CNT/MoSe2/C heterostructure with an expanded MoSe2 interlayer spacing for an efficient sodium storage. Adv. Energy Mater. 9(30), 1900567 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e685">73</a></sup>. Two-dimension semiconductors, particularly TMDs, have attracted tremendous attention as promising candidates for the next-generation energy storage devices. The attraction is owing to the better high conductivity, surface area (that provides storage surface sites), exceptional structural stability, and layered structure of TMDs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Ali, M. et al. 2D-TMDs based electrode material for supercapacitor applications. Int. J. Energy Res. 46(15), 22336–22364 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e689">74</a></sup>. These characteristics candidate the TMDs to be more favorable contenders to store energy. It is worth mentioning that adjacent layers in TMDs materials are bounded with comparatively weak van der Waals (vdW) interactions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Cai, Q. et al. Monolayer-like lattice dynamics in bulk WSe2. Mater. Today Phys. 28, 100856 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e693">75</a></sup>. Moreover, the uniform layered structure has provided permeable channels for inserting/extracting Na<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup> ions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Liu, A. et al. Insight on cathodes chemistry for aqueous zinc-ion batteries: From reaction mechanisms, structural engineering, and modification strategies. Small 18(28), 2201011 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e701">76</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Zhang, C. et al. Progress and perspectives of 2D materials as anodes for potassium-ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 38, 354–378 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e704">77</a></sup>. Recently, some theoretical studies also indicated that TMDs monolayers could substantially accelerate ion diffusion and accommodate more ions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Jiang, D. et al. Flexible electronics based on 2D transition metal dichalcogenides. J. Mater. Chem. A 10, 89–121 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e709">78</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Mei, J. et al. 2D/2D heterostructures: Rational design for advanced batteries and electrocatalysis. Energy Environ. Mater. 5, 115–132 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e712">79</a></sup>. Molybdenum diselenide (MoSe<sub>2</sub>), among these TMDs, is regarded as a competitive anode material with an interlayer spacing of 6.5&nbsp;Å<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Li, Y. et al. Molecular engineering strategies toward molybdenum diselenide design for energy storage and conversion. Adv. Energy Mater. 12(45), 2202600 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e718">80</a></sup>, which facilitates large-size of PIBs (1.38&nbsp;Å) insertion/extraction and decreases the corresponding diffusion barrier<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Zeng, L. et al. Facile synthesis of ultra-small few-layer nanostructured MoSe2 embedded on N, P co-doped bio-carbon for high-performance half/full sodium-ion and potassium-ion batteries. Chem. Eur. J. 25(58), 13411–13421 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e722">81</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Liu, X. et al. In-depth mechanism understanding for potassium-ion batteries by electroanalytical methods and advanced in situ characterization techniques. Small Methods 5(12), 2101130 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e725">82</a></sup>. Therefore, to promote the structural stability and the electrical conductivity of MoSe<sub>2</sub>, great efforts have been made, such as designing the hierarchical structure and heteroatomic interface engineering<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wazir, M. B. et al. Review on 2D molybdenum diselenide (MoSe2) and its hybrids for green hydrogen (H2) generation applications. ACS Omega 7(20), 16856–16865 (2022)." href="#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e731">83</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Dai, S. et al. Design strategies in metal chalcogenides anode materials for high-performance sodium-ion battery. Mater. Today Energy 12, 114–128 (2019)." href="#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e731_1">84</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Liu, S. et al. Recent advances and perspectives of battery-type anode materials for potassium ion storage. ACS Nano 15(12), 18931 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e734">85</a></sup>. Consequently, it could effectively suppress the volume changes of MoSe<sub>2</sub> and significantly increase the electron transport in the composite<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="Guo, W. et al. Ni3Se4@ MoSe2 composites for hydrogen evolution reaction. Appl. Sci. 9(23), 5035 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e741">86</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 87" title="Peng, H. et al. 2D heterolayer-structured MoSe2-carbon with fast kinetics for sodium-ion capacitors. Inorg. Chem. 62(4), 1602–1610 (2023)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e744">87</a></sup>. It is worth noting that the main disadvantages of MoSe<sub>2</sub> materials are their electronic conductivity and low instinct density during cycling. Meanwhile, integrating the MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheet with other low-cost conductive substrate materials is expected to increase the alkaline ion storage performance<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 88" title="Al-Tahan, M. A. et al. Modulating of MoSe2 functional plane via doping-defect engineering strategy for the development of conductive and electrocatalytic mediators in Li-S batteries. J. Energy Chem. 75, 512–523 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR88" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e752">88</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 89" title="Yu, J. et al. Manipulation of the MoO2/MoSe2 heterointerface boosting high rate and durability for sodium/potassium storage. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 14(32), 36592 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR89" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e755">89</a></sup>. Therefore, one of the effective strategies is coupling molybdenum diselenide and carbon materials to improve electrical conductivity and structural stability. Transition metal selenides have attracted attention as anode materials for SIBs due to their high theoretical capacity and electronic conductivity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 90" title="Zhang, Y. et al. Nanostructured metal chalcogenides for energy storage and electrocatalysis. Adv. Funct. Mater. 27(35), 1702317 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR90" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e759">90</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 91" title="Fan, H. et al. 1D to 3D hierarchical iron selenide hollow nanocubes assembled from FeSe2@ C core-shell nanorods for advanced sodium ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 10, 48–55 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR91" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e762">91</a></sup>. Nevertheless, the pronounced volume changes associated with transition metal selenide-based anode materials result in poor cycle stability during the repetitive insertion/extraction of SIBs. The creation of a low-dimensional structure holds promise as a solution, as it not only mitigates volume expansion but also offers additional active sites for the migration of Na<sup>+</sup><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 92" title="Chen, S. et al. Boosting sodium storage of Fe1–xS/MoS2 composite via heterointerface engineering. Nano-Micro Lett. 11, 1–14 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR92" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e768">92</a></sup>. Additionally, a common strategy to enhance the cycle stability of transition metal selenides involves their combination with other highly conductive electrodes, such as graphene, MXene, and carbon nanotubes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 93" title="Deng, Q. et al. Ultrathin cobalt nickel selenides (Co0.5Ni0.5Se2) nanosheet arrays anchoring on Ti3C2 MXene for high-performance Na+/K+ batteries. J. Colloid Interface Sci. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jcis.2022.06.073
                  
                 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR93" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e772">93</a></sup>. Among the various investigated anode materials, due to its distinctive structural advantages, MoSe<sub>2</sub> has garnered extensive attention as an anode material in energy storage applications<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 118" title="Zhang, Z. et al. Hierarchical MoSe2 nanosheets/reduced graphene oxide composites as anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries with enhanced electrochemical performance. ChemNanoMat 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/cnma.201500097
                  
                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR118" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e778">118</a></sup>. MoSe<sub>2</sub>, with its unique 2D layered  
structure and high specific capacity, is a promising electrode material for SIBs. MoSe<sub>2</sub> stands out among transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDCs) and similar compounds due to the significant role of Mo in conferring a metallic nature. The unique properties of the 2D layered framework, characterized by substantial layer distances, enhance the diffusion kinetics of Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>. However, the relatively low electrical conductivity imposes a limitation on electron transfer, leading to poor rate capability<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhao, Z. et al. Defective Bi2S3 anchored on CuS/C as an ultrafast and long-life anode for sodium-ion storage. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 15(3), 4011–4020 (2023)." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e791">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Liu, X. &amp; Ye, Z. Nitroaromatics as high-energy organic cathode materials for rechargeable alkali-ion (Li+, Na+, and K+) batteries. Adv. Energy Mater. 11(4), 2003281 (2021)." href="#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e791_1">28</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Eom, K. et al. Crystalline chlorinated contorted hexabenzocoronene: A universal organic anode for advanced alkali-ion batteries. J. Mater. Chem. A 9(36), 20607–20614 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e794">29</a></sup>. Nanostructure engineering strategies are extensively used to enhance Na<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup> storage characteristics of molybdenum chalcogenides. In contrast to bulk materials, engineering the nanostructure reduces the ion transfer distance, enhancing ion diffusion kinetics and relieving structural stress. This improvement promotes increased reaction activity and optimal utilization of active materials. For instance, Tao et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 94" title="Tao, J. et al. Rational designing of MoSe2 nanosheets in carbon framework for high-performance potassium-ion batteries. Chem. Eng. J. 448, 137658 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR94" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e803">94</a></sup> showed that carbon-coated MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets as anode for PIBs deliver a high-specific capacity of 258&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 300 cycles at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Li et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 95" title="Li, X. et al. Microstructures constructed by MoSe2/C nanoplates sheathed in N-doped carbon for efficient sodium (potassium) storage. J. Alloys Compds 890, 161746 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR95" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e813">95</a></sup> synthesized the MoSe<sub>2</sub>/C nano-plates sheathed in N-doped carbon (MoSe<sub>2</sub>/C@NC) as ideal anode material in the field of energy storage for Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>. The results showed a SIBs/PIBs storage capacity of 362 and 310&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h/g at 0.1&nbsp;A/g, respectively. Moreover, Kang et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 96" title="Kang, W. et al. Organic–inorganic assembly engineering of core–double-shell VSe 16/C@ N-C⊂ MoSe2 nanotubes for boosting Na+/K+ storage performance. J. Mater. Chem. A 10(35), 18185–18194 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR96" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e826">96</a></sup> created a core/shell nanotube structure (VSe 1.6/C@N–C<span class="stix">⊂</span>MoSe<sub>2</sub>, with VSe 1.6/C inner cores) as an anode material for Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>, it exhibited markedly enhanced high cycling stability. Recently, Zhang et al. synthesized a hierarchical nanorod structure (MoSe<sub>2</sub>/N–C) to evaluate the practical application of MoSe<sub>2</sub>/N-C anode for the charge/discharge process and maintaining the structural integrity of MoSe<sub>2</sub>. The results showed that the MoSe<sub>2</sub>/N-C anode materials has a superior high-rate capability and long-cycle performance for storing Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 97" title="Zhang, X. et al. Hierarchical interlayer-expanded MoSe2/N–C nanorods for high-rate and long-life sodium and potassium-ion batteries. Inorg. Chem. Front. 8(5), 1271–1278 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR97" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e849">97</a></sup>. Notwithstanding the latest improvements in MoSe<sub>2</sub>/C anode materials, optimizing the C/MoSe<sub>2</sub> structure is still in progress and worthy of further investigation. MXenes are expressed by the general formula M<sub>n+1</sub>X<sub>n</sub>T<sub>x</sub> (n = 1–3), where M is an early transition metal (such as Ti, Nb, V, etc.) X is C/N or a mixture of them, and T<sub>x</sub> represents oxygen [=O], hydroxyl [–OH] and fluorine [–F]<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 98" title="Laishram, D. et al. 2D transition metal carbides (MXenes) for applications in electrocatalysis. Heterog. Nanocatalysis Energy Environ Sustain. 1, 165–198 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR98" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e866">98</a></sup>. MXenes have been extensively investigated as metal electrode materials, capitalizing on their theoretically significant metal ion storage capacities and intriguing structural controllability<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 99" title="Zhang, C. J. et al. Oxidation stability of colloidal two-dimensional titanium carbides (MXenes). Chem. Mater. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.chemmater.7b00745
                  
                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR99" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e870">99</a></sup>. Meanwhile, The MXene substrate is highly conductive, this contributes to the effective reduction of MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheet aggregation and an increase in the conductivity of the electrode material. According to current developments for rechargeable batteries, 2D MXene materials are ideal hosts for LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs storage<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 100" title="Dong, G. et al. Three-dimensional Ti3C2Tx and MnS composites as anode materials for high performance alkalis (Li, Na, K) ion batteries. J. Colloid Interface Sci. 633, 468 (2023)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR100" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e876">100</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 101" title="Liu, S. et al. MXenes for metal-ion and metal-sulfur batteries: Synthesis, properties, and electrochemistry. Mater. Rep. Energy 2(1), 100077 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR101" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e879">101</a></sup>. Given their numerous attractive qualities, including substantial interlayer spacing and a minimal Na+/K+ diffusion barrier, there exist considerable possibilities for developing electrodes specifically tailored for high-performance SIBs/PIBs. Besides, due to surface functional groups with a negative charge, they are used for the selective separation of ions in different sizes and charges<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Hong, S. et al. Ion-selective separation using MXene-based membranes: A review. ACS Mater. Lett. 5(2), 341–356 (2023)." href="#ref-CR102" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e884">102</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Li, J. et al. Recent advances of two-dimensional (2D) MXenes and phosphorene for high-performance rechargeable batteries. ChemSusChem 3(6), 1047–1070 (2020)." href="#ref-CR103" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e884_1">103</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Dong, Y. et al. Recent advances and promise of MXene-based nanostructures for high-performance metal ion batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 30(47), 2000706 (2020)." href="#ref-CR104" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e884_2">104</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 105" title="Mozafari, M. et al. Ion-selective MXene-based membranes: Current status and prospects. Adv. Mater. Technol. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/admt.202001189
                  
                 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR105" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e887">105</a></sup>. For example, Wu et al. reported the MoS<sub>2</sub> nanosheets on MXene stabilized via a carbon-based nanoplate (C), which displayed significant electrochemical properties as an ideal anode material for LIBs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 106" title="Wu, X. et al. Stabilizing the MXenes by carbon nanoplating for developing hierarchical nanohybrids with efficient lithium storage and hydrogen evolution capability. Adv. Mater. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201607017
                  
                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR106" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e893">106</a></sup>. Also, Cao et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 107" title="Cao, J. et al. Ti3C2Tx MXene conductive layers supported bio-derived fex- 1Sex/MXene/carbonaceous nanoribbons for high-performance half/full sodium-ion and potassium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 33(34), 2101535 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR107" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e897">107</a></sup> designed the MXene@N-doped carbonaceous nanofiber structure as a novel electrode material for high-performance SIBs and PIBs. They found that this porous nanostructure promotes the transport and conduction of SIBs and PIBs and fully uses the intrinsic advantages of the 2D material. And also, Sun et al. designed the carbonaceous nanofiber structure (MXene@N-doped) as the anode for application in high-performance energy storage for SIBs and PIBs. Their results showed that this anode material can significantly enhance the capacitive storage of AMIBs and provides efficient charge transfer in the electrode<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 108" title="Sun, Z. et al. Microbe-assisted assembly of Ti3C2Tx MXene on fungi-derived nanoribbon heterostructures for ultrastable sodium and potassium ion storage. ACS Nano 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.0c10491
                  
                 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR108" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e901">108</a></sup>. Xu et al. also investigated the innovative ultrafast network electrode composed of MXene/MoSe<sub>2</sub>, which is synthesized via a simple hydrothermal method for energy storage devices and SIBs. The results revealed that the created cells demonstrate a high degree of reversibility capacities and excellent electrochemical performance of the hybrid materials, especially at high currents<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 109" title="Xu, E. et al. Ultrafast kinetics net electrode assembled via MoSe2/MXene heterojunction for high-performance sodium-ion batteries. Chem. Eng. J. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cej.2019.123839
                  
                 (2020)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR109" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e908">109</a></sup>. Besides, Liang et al. reported a three-dimensional hierarchical structure of MoSe<sub>2</sub> with nitrogen and fluorine co-doped carbon (MoSe<sub>2</sub>/NFC) structure which facilitates Li<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction. Their findings demonstrated excellent rate performance and an exceptionally long cycling life, making them suitable for use in LIBs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 110" title="Liang, Q. et al. Three-dimensional hierarchical MoSe2/N, F Co-doped carbon heterostructure assembled by ultrathin nanosheets for advanced lithium-ion batteries. ACS Sustain. Chem. Eng. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acssuschemeng.0c04719
                  
                 (2020)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR110" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e918">110</a></sup>. Recently, various computational studies have been examined to facilitate the rationalization of experimentally observed phenomena. For example, molecular dynamics (MD) simulations can predict how selected atoms in various LIBs/SIBs/PIBs systems will move over time based on an overall insight into the physics governing interatomic interactions. Herein, we can gain further insights into alkali ions (Li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>) transport mechanisms and the mobility of migration of Li<sup>+</sup>, Na<sup>+</sup>, and K<sup>+</sup> toward the anode material with MD open-source code for the Large-scale Atomic/Molecular Massively Parallel Simulator (LAMMPS). Hence, to assess its suitability as an anode for PIBs/NIs/LIBs systems, we examined the properties of the system, including energies, the root means square deviation, the mean square displacement, and the radial distribution function. The results evidence that rationally designing the carbon-covered MXene/MoSe<sub>2</sub> can dramatically improve their LIBs/SIBs/KIBs storage performances. Generally, our objective in this regard is to answer the following question: Did the interface of MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets, MXene flakes, and carbon layer as anodes help to promote charge transfer and improve structural durability for energy storage for LIBs/SIBs/PIBs by MD simulation code LAMMPS?</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Materials and methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2">Materials and methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><p>Herein, we investigated a well-designed structural of carbon-coated MoSe<sub>2</sub> with the MXene hybrid nanosheets (MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C) as the anode material for LIBs/SIBs/PIBs. It is worth mentioning that the initial geometry of anode material is taken from the X-ray data by Huang et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 111" title="Huang, H. et al. Carbon-coated MoSe2/MXene hybrid nanosheets for superior potassium storage. ACS Nano 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.8b09548
                  
                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR111" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e952">111</a></sup> work. The design of the MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C as an anode material is illustrated in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig1">1</a>. In this regard, MXene nanosheets is used as a conductive substrate; thus, MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets are positioned vertically on the MXene surface to obtain hybrid MXene/MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets. It is noteworthy that the MXene flakes are anchored to the MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets via strong covalent bonds, which is significant for improving the hybrid structure’s stabilizing and promoting the kinetics of the migration of electrons and alkali ions throughout charge and discharge processes. In addition, the formation of Ti–O–Mo through covalent bonding at the interface between MXene and MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets enhances the interaction between the two components. In addition, the MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets have covered the surface of the MXene flake to form a 3D network of interconnected porous structures. Moreover, the carbon layer evenly covers MXene/MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanocomposite, amplifying the 2D nano-structure and increasing the overall conductivity. Thus, three simulation systems are designed as promising anode materials for Li<sup>+</sup>, Na<sup>+</sup>, and K<sup>+</sup> and randomly distributed around the MXene structure. Most importantly, the key point is achieving fast LIBs/SIBs/PIBs diffusion kinetics in the MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C interlayer. Furthermore, this strategy of the hierarchical 2D nanosheet structure of MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C electrode is promising for developing a high-performance with potential applications in supercapacitors and batteries.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Figure 1"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 1</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig1_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig1" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig1_HTML.png" alt="figure 1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="417"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p>The structures of the anode materials.
