(<b>a</b>) PIBs system (<b>b</b>) SIBs system (<b>c</b>) LIBs system.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 1" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Comprehending the alkali-metal extraction/insertion mechanism is crucial in solid-state chemistry and holds significance in utilizing it as positive electrode materials for LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs. MXenes have undergone exploration as electrode materials for storing Na<sup>+</sup><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Buczek, S. et al. Rational design of titanium carbide MXene electrode architectures for hybrid capacitive deionization. Energy Environ. Mater. 3(3), 398–404 (2020)." href="#ref-CR112" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1016">112</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Luo, J. et al. Atomic sulfur covalently engineered interlayers of Ti3C2 MXene for ultra-fast sodium-ion storage by enhanced pseudocapacitance. Adv. Funct. Mater. 29(10), 1808107 (2019)." href="#ref-CR113" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1016_1">113</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 114" title="Sharma, G. et al. Calorimetric study of alkali metal ion (K+, Na+, Li+) exchange in a clay-like MXene. J. Phys. Chem. C. 121(28), 15145 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR114" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1019">114</a></sup>. It’s noteworthy that the only work corresponding to Ti<sub>2</sub>CTx used as an anode electrode for SIBs was reported by Yamada and co-workers. The findings from Yin et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 115" title="Yin, F. et al. Flexible MoSe2/MXene films for Li/Na-ion hybrid capacitors. J. Power Sources 488, 229452 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR115" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1025">115</a></sup>, Yang et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 116" title="Yang, X. et al. Porous hollow carbon spheres decorated with molybdenum diselenide nanosheets as anodes for highly reversible lithium and sodium storage. Nanoscale 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/c5nr01909e
                  
                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR116" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1029">116</a></sup>, and Li group<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 117" title="Li, J. et al. Metal selenides find plenty of space in architecting advanced sodium/potassium ion batteries. Small 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/smll.202305021
                  
                 (2024)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR117" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1033">117</a></sup> demonstrate a complete reaction from Li<sub>2</sub>Se to MoSe<sub>2</sub>, as opposed to Se, throughout the charging process. The regeneration of MoSe<sub>2</sub> serves as evidence for the reversible reaction with Li<sup>+</sup>, thereby confirming the reversibility outlined in Eq.&nbsp;(<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="equation anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Equ1">1</a>) during the discharge/charge process.</p><div id="Equ1" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{MoSe}}_{{2}} + {\text{4Li}}^{ + } + {\text{4e }} \leftrightarrow {\text{ Mo }} + {\text{ 2Li}}_{{2}} {\text{Se}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (1)
                </div></div><p>The sodium storage mechanism in MoSe<sub>2</sub><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 117" title="Li, J. et al. Metal selenides find plenty of space in architecting advanced sodium/potassium ion batteries. Small 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/smll.202305021
                  
                 (2024)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR117" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1129">117</a></sup> is contingent upon the discharge potential cut-off. Specifically, when the cut-off voltage is placed higher than 0.5&nbsp;V, an intercalation reaction occurs in the material, as defined by Eq.&nbsp;(<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="equation anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Equ6">6</a>). Conversely, when the cut-off is set below 0.5&nbsp;V, a conversion reaction takes place, as outlined in Eq.&nbsp;(<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="equation anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Equ7">7</a>). Despite conversion reactions, the MoSe<sub>2</sub> anode experiences an enhancement in a specific capacity; meanwhile, it results in the collapse of the layered structure in the composites, it causes the layered structure in the composites to break down, contributing to inferior cycling performance<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 118" title="Zhang, Z. et al. Hierarchical MoSe2 nanosheets/reduced graphene oxide composites as anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries with enhanced electrochemical performance. ChemNanoMat 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/cnma.201500097
                  
                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR118" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1141">118</a></sup>. The findings lead to the conclusion that the regulation of the cut-off discharge voltage is essential for optimizing overall performance.</p><p>A summary of the reaction mechanisms (Eqs.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="equation anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Equ2">2</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="equation anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Equ3">3</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 116" title="Yang, X. et al. Porous hollow carbon spheres decorated with molybdenum diselenide nanosheets as anodes for highly reversible lithium and sodium storage. Nanoscale 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/c5nr01909e
                  
                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR116" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1154">116</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 117" title="Li, J. et al. Metal selenides find plenty of space in architecting advanced sodium/potassium ion batteries. Small 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/smll.202305021
                  
                 (2024)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR117" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1157">117</a></sup> of TMSes materials for SIBs/PIB is in the following:</p><div id="Equ2" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{MaSe}}_{{\text{b}}} + {\text{xNa}}^{ + } /{\text{K}}^{ + } + {\text{ xe}}^{ - } \leftrightarrow {\text{ Na}}_{{\text{x}}} {\text{M}}_{{\text{a}}} {\text{Se}}_{{\text{b}}} \left( {{\text{K}}_{{\text{x}}} {\text{M}}_{{\text{a}}} {\text{Se}}_{{\text{b}}} } \right)$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (2)
                </div></div><div id="Equ3" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{Na}}_{{\text{x}}} {\text{M}}_{{\text{a}}} {\text{Se}}_{{\text{b}}} \left( {{\text{K}}_{{\text{x}}} {\text{M}}_{{\text{a}}} {\text{Se}}_{{\text{b}}} } \right) \, + \, \left( {{\text{2b}} - {\text{x}}} \right){\text{ Na}}^{ + } /{\text{K}}^{ + } + \, \left( {{\text{2b}} - {\text{x}}} \right){\text{ e}}^{ - } \leftrightarrow {\text{aM}} + {\text{bNa}}_{{2}} {\text{Se }}\left( {{\text{K}}_{{2}} {\text{Se}}} \right)$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (3)
                </div></div><p>According to the Yin co-worker’s<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 115" title="Yin, F. et al. Flexible MoSe2/MXene films for Li/Na-ion hybrid capacitors. J. Power Sources 488, 229452 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR115" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1465">115</a></sup> analysis, the mechanism for Na<sup>+</sup> storage can be elucidated through the following reaction formulas:</p><div id="Equ4" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{MoSe}}_{{2}} + {\text{4Na}}^{ + } + {\text{4e }} \to {\text{Mo }} + {\text{ 2Na}}_{{2}} {\text{S}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (4)
                </div></div><div id="Equ5" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{Na}}_{{2}} {\text{Se }} \leftrightarrow {\text{ Se }} + {\text{ 2Na}}^{ + } + {\text{2e}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (5)
                </div></div><p>To Understanding the alkali-metal extraction/insertion mechanism<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 116" title="Yang, X. et al. Porous hollow carbon spheres decorated with molybdenum diselenide nanosheets as anodes for highly reversible lithium and sodium storage. Nanoscale 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/c5nr01909e
                  
                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR116" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1612">116</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 117" title="Li, J. et al. Metal selenides find plenty of space in architecting advanced sodium/potassium ion batteries. Small 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/smll.202305021
                  
                 (2024)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR117" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1615">117</a></sup> holds significant importance not only in solid-state chemistry but also in the application of these materials utilized as electrode for LIBs, NIBs, and KIBs.</p><div id="Equ6" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{MoSe}}_{{2}} + {\text{xNa}}^{ + } \leftrightarrow {\text{ Na}}_{{\text{x}}} {\text{MoSe}}_{{2}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (6)
                </div></div><div id="Equ7" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{Na}}_{{\text{x}}} {\text{MoSe}}_{{2}} + {4 } - {\text{ xNa}}^{ + } \leftrightarrow {\text{ Mo }} + {\text{ 2Na}}_{{2}} {\text{Se}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (7)
                </div></div><p>The K storage mechanism of the MoSe<sub>2</sub> in the initial cycle closely parallels that of MoSe<sub>2</sub>/Na. More precisely, K<sup>+</sup> intercalation reactions occur at voltages exceeding 0.53&nbsp;V, whereas below this threshold, conversion reactions are triggered<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 119" title="Zhong, F. et al. Confining MoSe2 nanosheets into N-doped hollow porous carbon microspheres for fast-charged and long-life potassium-ion storage. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 13(50), 59882 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR119" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1769">119</a></sup>. In the following cycles, the MoSe<sub>2</sub>/K mechanism deviates from that of MoSe<sub>2</sub>/Na. The Lu group conducted ex situ XRD, Raman, and TEM analyses, revealing that the primary discharge product is K<sub>5</sub>Se<sub>3</sub>. In contrast, the charge product comprises MoSe<sub>2</sub>, Mo<sub>15</sub>Se<sub>19</sub>, and Se<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 119" title="Zhong, F. et al. Confining MoSe2 nanosheets into N-doped hollow porous carbon microspheres for fast-charged and long-life potassium-ion storage. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 13(50), 59882 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR119" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1789">119</a></sup>.</p><p>In contrast to the pristine MoSe<sub>2</sub> electrode, the MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene electrode exhibits significantly enhanced cycling performance at high rates in Na<sup>+</sup> and Li<sup>+</sup> half cells. This improvement can be attributed, in part, to the confining influence of the MXene.</p><p>Notably, we have investigated an innovative approach to designing Ti-based MXene@MoSe@/C electrode materials for advanced LIBs/SIBs and PIBs storage using the LAMMPS package.</p><p>The details about the simulation box size and the total number of alkali ions for each of the systems are presented in Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Tab1">1</a>. The initial atomic coordinates are arranged using packing optimization through the Packmol program for molecular dynamics simulations<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 120" title="Silva, L. A. &amp; Correia, J. C. G. GEMS-Pack: A graphical user interface for the packmol program. J. Chem. Inf. Model. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.jcim.9b00740
                  
                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR120" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1813">120</a></sup>. Eventually, in this simulation, the periodic boundary condition (PBC) is applied along the X, Y and Z-axis, with a box dimension of 4 × 4 × 9&nbsp;nm<sup>3</sup>. Furthermore, the periodic boundary conditions are evaluated in the x and y directions. At each time step, the forces from the MD particles that the fix acts on are applied to the ions, and the ions properties are calculated.</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-1"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab1" data-test="table-caption">Table 1 Detail of the simulation boxes used in this study.</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/tables/1" aria-label="Full size table 1"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>For the initial structure design of the simulation, we utilized the ATOMSK program<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 121" title="Hirel, P. Atomsk: A tool for manipulating and converting atomic data files. Comput. Phys. Commun. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cpc.2015.07.012
                  
                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR121" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1949">121</a></sup>. Visualization and snapshots of the simulation are obtained utilizing VMD (visual molecular dynamics)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 122" title="Humphrey, W. et al. VMD: Visual molecular dynamics. J. Mol. Graph. 14(1), 33–38 (1996)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR122" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1953">122</a></sup> package and the graphics software package Open Visualization Tool (OVITO)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 123" title="Stukowski, A. Visualization and analysis of atomistic simulation data with OVITO–the open visualization tool. Model. Simul. Mater. Sci. Eng. 18(1), 015012 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR123" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1957">123</a></sup>. All MD simulations of LIBs/SIBs/PIBs are performed using the LAMMPS program<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 124" title="Thompson, A. P. et al. LAMMPS-a flexible simulation tool for particle-based materials modeling at the atomic, meso, and continuum scales. Comput. Phys. Commun. 271, 108171 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR124" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1961">124</a></sup> (version 2 Mar 2020), which is designed by Sandia National Laboratories (SNL)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 125" title="Thompson, A. P. &amp; Trott, C. R. A Brief Description of the Kokkos Implementation of the SNAP Potential in ExaMiniMD (Sandia National Lab, 2017)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR125" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1965">125</a></sup>, a very customizable molecular dynamics simulation software. In addition, for anode material, we need an attractive interaction to hold the components together and repulsive to prevent the overlap of the nanostructure. Therefore, the Lennard–Jones potential is often used to model this behavior in simulations<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 126" title="Felipe, J. Thermodynamic behaviour of homonuclear and heteronuclear Lennard-Jones chains with association sites from simulation and theory. Mol. Phys. 92(1), 135–150 (1997)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR126" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e1970">126</a></sup>. The MD simulation results are strongly dependent on the choice of force field for interactions between atoms. This simulation is investigated with a Lenard Jones (LJ) force field, for anode materials. This force field quantifies energy in kcal mol<sup>−1</sup>, aligning with the real units. Notably, the optical atomic style for simulating batteries in the LAMMPS software is set to full. The energy potential is described through valence-bonded and nonbonded interactions.</p><p>E = E<sub>R</sub> + E<sub>θ</sub> + E<sub>φ</sub> + E<sub>ω</sub> + E<sub>vdw</sub> + E<sub>elc</sub> where E<sub>R</sub> represents valence interactions, E<sub>θ</sub> corresponds to bond angle bending, E<sub>Φ</sub> denotes dihedral angle torsion, E<sub>ω</sub> accounts for the inversion term, E<sub>vdw</sub> covers interactions of vdW, and E<sub>elc</sub> represents the electrostatic term. The following details (Eq.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="equation anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Equ8">8</a>) are illustrated the nonbonded interactions (vdW forces) with potential LJ, where r<sub>ij</sub> represents the distance between the interacting particles, and σ and ε determine the length scale and scale of the interaction strength, respectively.</p><p>The cut-off radius is shown with “<span class="mathjax-tex">\({{\text{r}}}_{{\text{c}}}\)</span>”, set as 12–15&nbsp;Å in all simulations. The parameters σ and ε depend on the type of atoms in the simulated structure<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 127" title="Farhadi, B. et al. Influence of contact electrode and light power on the efficiency of tandem perovskite solar cell: Numerical simulation. Sol. Energy 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.solener.2021.08.043
                  
                 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR127" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e2035">127</a></sup>, In this particular model, the nonbonded interactions, specifically the van der Waals forces, through the Lennard–Jones potential are represented in the following:</p><p>The potential is defined as:</p><div id="Equ8" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{U}}\left( {r_{ij} } \right) = {4}\upvarepsilon \left[ { \, \left( {{\raise0.7ex\hbox{$\sigma $} \!\mathord{\left/ {\vphantom {\sigma {r_{ij} }}}\right.\kern-0pt} \!\lower0.7ex\hbox{${r_{ij} }$}}} \right)^{12} - \left( {{\raise0.7ex\hbox{$\sigma $} \!\mathord{\left/ {\vphantom {\sigma {r_{ij} }}}\right.\kern-0pt} \!\lower0.7ex\hbox{${r_{ij} }$}}} \right)^{6} } \right]\quad {\text{if}}\,r_{ij} \le r_{c}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (8)
                </div></div><p>The 1/r<sup>6</sup> term is related to vdW attraction, while the 1/r<sup>12</sup> term is related to the repulsion between electron clouds.</p><p>For L–J interactions between different atom types, parameters ε<sub>i,j</sub> and σ<sub>i,j</sub> are calculated using Lorentz − Berthelot combining rules<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 128" title="Galliero, G. et al. Estimation of thermodiffusion in ternary alkane mixtures using molecular dynamics simulations and an irreversible thermodynamic theory. High Temp. High Press. 38, 315–328 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR128" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e2216">128</a></sup>:</p><div id="Equ9" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$$\varepsilon_{ij} = \sqrt {\upvarepsilon _{ij} \, \upvarepsilon _{ij} }$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (9)
                </div></div><div id="Equ10" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$$\sigma_{ij} = \frac{{\sigma_{ij} + \sigma_{ij} }}{2}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (10)
                </div></div><p>where ε and <span class="mathjax-tex">\(\upsigma\)</span> refer to the Lennard–Jones energy and distance are applied to estimate the parameters for atom-pairs. The values Lennard–Jones parameters of the current study are presented in Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Tab2">2</a>.</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-2"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab2" data-test="table-caption">Table 2 Lennard–Jones Pair Potential Parameters.</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/tables/2" aria-label="Full size table 2"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Interatomic interactions, such as dihedral, bond strength, inversion, angle torsion, terms bond strength, and bond-angle bend for a single atom, can be computed using the equations provided below:</p><div id="Equ11" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{E }} = \frac{1}{2}{\text{ K}}_{{\text{r}}} \left( {{\text{r}} - {\text{r}}_{0} } \right)$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (11)
                </div></div><p>The harmonic oscillator constant used in the MD simulation is 300&nbsp;(Kcal/mol)/A<sup>2</sup> where K<sub>r</sub> represents the harmonic oscillator constant and r<sub>0</sub> is the atomic bond length. Moreover, the angle energies are obtained from the following equation:</p><div id="Equ12" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{E }} = \frac{1}{2} {\text{K}}_{\uptheta } \left( {\uptheta -\uptheta _{0} } \right)^{{2}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (12)
                </div></div><p>The oscillator’s harmonic angle constant (<span class="mathjax-tex">\({K}_{\theta }\)</span>) is equal to 100 (Kcal/mol)/θ<sup>2</sup> for different angles, where θ<sub>0</sub> represents the equilibrium angle. The energy was minimized using the conjugate gradient method.</p><p>After that, Newton’s second law of the equation is utilized as the gradient of the potential function to describe the evolvement of particles as a function of time.</p><div id="Equ13" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{F}}_{{\text{i}}} = \sum\nolimits_{{{\text{i}} \ne {\text{j}}}} {{\text{F}}_{{{\text{ij}}}} = {\text{m}}_{{\text{i}}} } \frac{{{\text{d}}^{2} {\text{r}}_{{\text{i}}} }}{{{\text{dt}}^{2} }} = {\text{m}}_{{\text{i}}} \frac{{{\text{dv}}_{{\text{i}}} }}{{{\text{dt}}}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (13)
                </div></div><div id="Equ14" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{F}}_{{{\text{ij}}}} = - {\text{grad}}\,{\text{V}}_{{{\text{ij}}}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (14)
                </div></div><p>where <span class="mathjax-tex">\({r}_{i}\)</span> is the position of atom i, m<sub>i</sub> is atomic mass, V<sub>ij</sub> is the potential function, and dt is MD time step. It is worth mentioning that the Velocity-Verlet algorithm owing to its stability and simplicity, fulfills motion equations’ association, in common in MD simulations.</p><p>In Eq. (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="equation anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Equ9">9</a>), the momentum <span class="mathjax-tex">\(({{\text{P}}}_{\mathfrak{i}}\)</span>) can be described as below:</p><div id="Equ15" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{P}}_{{\text{i}}} = {\text{ m}}_{{\text{i}}} {\text{v}}_{{\text{i}}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (15)
                </div></div><p>The total energy (E) is representable through the Hamiltonian of atomic structures. When considering N atoms, it can be formulated as follows:</p><div id="Equ16" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{H}}\left( {{\text{r}},{\text{ p}}} \right) \, = { 1}/{2}\sum\nolimits_{i} P + {\text{ U }}(r_{1 } + r_{2} ) = {\text{E}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (16)
                </div></div><p>The total forces acting on each atom are calculated using the potential function, outlined as follows:</p><div id="Equ17" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$$\frac{dU}{{dr_{i} }} = - m_{i} a_{i} = - F_{i}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (17)
                </div></div><p>In these simulations, the equations of motion can be solved using the Verlet algorithm. This computational method is described as follows<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 129" title="Asgari, A. et al. Develop molecular dynamics method to simulate the flow and thermal domains of H2O/Cu nanofluid in a nanochannel affected by an external electric field. Int. J. Thermophys. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10765-020-02708-6
                  
                 (2020)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR129" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e3221">129</a></sup>:</p><div id="Equa" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$$\begin{gathered} {\text{r }}({\text{t }} + \Delta t) = {\text{r}}\left( {\text{t}} \right) + {\text{v}}\left( {\text{t}} \right) + \Delta t + {1}/{\text{2 a}}\left( {\text{t}} \right) \, \Delta {\text{t}}^{{2}} + {\text{O}}\Delta {\text{t}}^{{4}} \hfill \\ {\text{v }}({\text{t }} + \Delta t) = {\text{ v}}\left( {\text{t}} \right) \, + {\text{a}}\left( {\text{t}} \right) \, + {\text{ a}}({\text{t }} + \Delta t)^{2} + \Delta t + {\text{O}}\Delta {\text{t}}^{2} \hfill \\ \end{gathered}$$</span></div></div><p>Furthermore, the Gaussian distribution employed for estimating the temperature of atoms can be expressed using the equation below:</p><div id="Equ18" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$$3/2K_{B} {\text{T}} = {1}/{\text{N}}_{{{\text{atom}}}} \sum\nolimits_{i = 1}^{N} {\frac{1}{2} mv_{i}^{2} }$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (18)
                </div></div><p>Following energy minimization, in this step, the Nose–Hoover thermostat is used to stabilize the temperature of the atomic system at T = 300&nbsp;K as the starting conditions, using a time step of 1 fs, to eliminate any hot spots in the initial geometry, the NVT ensemble is used. Notably, the migration of AMIBs to the active sites of the anode material is facilitated by the electric field effect. Consequently, an external electric field of approximately 1.5&nbsp;Vnm<sup>−1</sup> is applied in the current study to improve system performance.</p><p>The Particle–Particle Particle-Mesh (PPPM) method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 130" title="Luty, B. A. &amp; van Gunsteren, W. F. Calculating electrostatic interactions using the particle- particle particle- mesh method with nonperiodic long-range interactions. J. Phys. Chem. 100(7), 2581 (1996)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR130" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e3605">130</a></sup> is applied to the behavior of long-range electrostatic interactions. During the simulation, all systems are simulated in a canonical ensemble; and the nano-anode materials is equilibrated for 10&nbsp;ns.</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Result and discussion"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec3-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec3">Result and discussion</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec3-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">MD simulation</h3><p>Molecular dynamics (MD) simulation is a useful tool to study diffusion processes in battery electrode materials, and the LAMMPS is a powerful MD simulation developed<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 131" title="Luo, C. &amp; Sommer, J.-U. Coding coarse grained polymer model for LAMMPS and its application to polymer crystallization. Comput. Phys. Commun. 180(8), 1382–1391 (2009)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR131" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e3621">131</a></sup>. LAMMPS is a molecular dynamics code designed for parallel platforms, with a focus on efficient execution, particularly in handling long-range coulomb interactions and developed by Plimpton et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 132" title="Plimpton, S. J. &amp; Thompson, A. P. Computational aspects of many-body potentials. MRS Bull. 37(5), 513–552 (2012)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR132" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e3625">132</a></sup>. In this regard, MD simulations for anode material are performed using the LAMMPS program, which hosts 30 alkaline ions (li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup>). The LAMMPS MD code has been carried out to understand the ability of the 2D carbon-coated anode nanosheets for superior LIBs, SIBs, and PIBs storage. The high pseudo-capacitive contribution of the prevention of self-aggregation in MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene with a carbon layer is primarily attributed to its two-dimensional structure. Additionally, it offers a substantial surface area that effectively facilitates the adsorption and desorption of alkali ions (K<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup>/Li<sup>+</sup>) throughout the charge and discharge cycles.</p><p>Our simulations have been divided into three setups (see Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Tab1">1</a>): (a) MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C for LIBs; (b) MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C for SIBs; (c) MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C for PIBs. The initial and final snapshots of the molecular structures of the LIBs/SIBs/PIBs models during 10 ns MD simulations are shown in Figs.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig1">1</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig2">2</a>. It’s worth noting that the distance between the carbon layer cover and the MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets after full optimization for anode material design is about 6.42&nbsp;Å. Additionally, the distance between each layer of the MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets is roughly 20&nbsp;Å. The distance between the AMIBs and Mexene is approximately ~ 20&nbsp;Å, and the interatomic distance varies from 4 to 5.5&nbsp;Å. The great capability and stability of energy storage of the MoSe<sub>2</sub>@MXene via carbon layer as anode could be attributed to a hybrid nanostructure by rational design and coupling with conductive electrodes. It’s important to note that the volume variation occurring at the anode while loading ions is crucial. Excessive changes in volume can potentially harm the battery’s structure and raise safety issues.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-2" data-title="Figure 2"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig2" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 2</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/2" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig2_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig2" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig2_HTML.png" alt="figure 2" loading="lazy" width="685" height="305"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-2-desc"><p>The snapshots of the final anode structures. (<b>a</b>) PIBs system (<b>b</b>) SIBs system (<b>c</b>) LIBs systems.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 2" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>As seen in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig2">2</a>, less swelling occurred for the anode systems because Li<sup>+</sup>, Na<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup> are preferentially migrated in the surface regions of the anode material, giving it a higher density. Overall, most SIBs and LIBs migrate around the surface of the MXene flakes and MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets interface. On the other hand, the difference in the adsorption of PIBs between the pores of anode material and the top or inner location of the anode is greater than that of Na<sup>+</sup> and Li<sup>+</sup>, indicating a higher preferential tendency to migrate toward the carbon layer.</p><p>Meanwhile, because of the ionic size difference (Li<sup>+</sup>: 0.76&nbsp;Å, Na<sup>+</sup>: 0.97&nbsp;Å, K<sup>+</sup>: 1.38&nbsp;Å), it leads to a decrease in diffusion and an increase in the penetration of LIBs compared to SIBs or PIBs during charge/discharge. Thus, pores’ shape and size directly influence alkali ion migration to 2D nanostructure. However, the anions tend to move towards the anode, marking the practical end of the charge cycle at 10 ns. The average of the potential energy of alkaline ions with anode material show varying negative values in the following sequence: system-SIB &gt; system-PIB &gt; system-LIB (are about ~ − 2030/41 &gt; − 912/36 &gt; − 713.65&nbsp;kcal&nbsp;mol<sup>−1</sup>). And also, the interaction energies of the studied systems is illustrated in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig3">3</a>. As seen, the potential energy of Na<sup>+</sup> is more negative than that of Li<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup>, which seems Na<sup>+</sup> to be significantly interacting with the surface of the anode material; this behavior may be related to the mobility and size of the ions. Following the migration process of LIBs/SIBs/PIBs toward the anode material, it is observed that the energy of Li<sup>+</sup> is lower than that of other ions, which indicates that Li<sup>+</sup> are more mobile than that Na<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup>. Worthwhile to be noted that the MXene has high electrical conductivity and suitable intracavity spacing for LIBs. So Li<sup>+</sup>, during the charge/discharge process, can easily move inner or outside the anode material without any barriers. Therefore, due to the smaller size/weight and lower mass of the Li<sup>+</sup>, the LIBs-system allocated less energy than other systems. Indeed, compared to Li<sup>+</sup>, Na<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup> have larger ionic radii and, thus, lower charge density. A larger radius indicates less mobility and less ion transport; thus, K<sup>+</sup> is strongly adsorbed to nano-anode materials compared to Li<sup>+</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup>. This result can be ascribed to the distinctive feature of MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C, along with the excellent mobility of Na<sup>+</sup>. Notably, this unique anode not only offers well-prepared storage locations for Na<sup>+</sup> than Li<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>, but also diminishes local current density, thereby governing the deposition behavior of Na<sup>+</sup><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 133" title="Liu, M. et al. Dual mechanism for sodium based energy storage. Small 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/smll.202206922
                  
                 (2023)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR133" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e3776">133</a></sup>. The central part of our composite material, MoSe<sub>2</sub>/Mo<sub>2</sub>CTx/C, contained of Se–Mo–Se layers. Notwithstanding that, the Se and Mo atoms formed via covalent bonds within each layer, the layers with themselves held together through weak vdW forces. This layered structure was particularly favorable for the entry of Na<sup>+</sup> into the MoSe<sub>2</sub> interlayer space. Furthermore, due to the 2D nanostructure of MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C electrode, the reduced Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion pathway and the ample storage sites have been supplied. Besides, the experimental work of Huang et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 111" title="Huang, H. et al. Carbon-coated MoSe2/MXene hybrid nanosheets for superior potassium storage. ACS Nano 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.8b09548
                  
                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR111" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e3793">111</a></sup>, presented the Carbon-Coated MXene@MoSe<sub>2</sub> as a material for storing K<sup>+</sup>. Their results identified with an outstanding rate performance with 183&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 10.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and a high reversible capacity of 355&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 200&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles. Beside, Yin and co-workers<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 115" title="Yin, F. et al. Flexible MoSe2/MXene films for Li/Na-ion hybrid capacitors. J. Power Sources 488, 229452 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR115" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e3811">115</a></sup> innovatively crafted a sandwich-structured MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene film to serve as an anode for Na<sup>+</sup>/Li<sup>+</sup> capacitors. The electrode design, characterized by the sandwich structure in MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene, exhibits a notably elevated after 100 cycles discharge capacity of 281&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="Figure 3"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 3</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/3" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig3_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig3" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig3_HTML.png" alt="figure 3" loading="lazy" width="685" height="516"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-3-desc"><p>The potential energy of the studied systems. For the SIBs, PIBs and LIBs anode. The error bars represent the standard deviations of the data.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/3" data-track-dest="link:Figure3 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 3" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5">Root mean square deviation</h3><p>The stability of the artificial anode material for the studied systems, such as LIBs/SIBs/PIBs, can be investigated by viewing the time dependence root mean square deviation (RMSD). This study serves dual purposes: validating the accuracy of our design and ensuring that our systems are in a state of conformational equilibrium. The difference between the initial and the final configuration is measured by the root mean square deviation (RMSD), presented by Eq.&nbsp;(<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig6">6</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 134" title="Arnittali, M. et al. Structure of biomolecules through molecular dynamics simulations. Procedia Comput. Sci. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.procs.2019.08.181
                  
                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR134" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e3854">134</a></sup>:</p><div id="Equ19" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{RMSD}} = \sqrt { {{\sum\nolimits_{i = 1}^{N} {m\left( {r_{i} - r_{ref} } \right)^{2} } } \mathord{\left/ {\vphantom {{\sum\nolimits_{i = 1}^{N} {m\left( {r_{i} - r_{ref} } \right)^{2} } } {\sum\nolimits_{i = 1}^{N} {m_{i} } }}} \right. \kern-0pt} {\sum\nolimits_{i = 1}^{N} {m_{i} } }}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (19)
                </div></div><p>where r<sub>i</sub> (r<sub>i,x</sub>, r<sub>i,y</sub>, r<sub>i,z</sub>) is the coordinates of atom i at a certain instance, r<sub>ref</sub> (r<sub>ref,x</sub>, r<sub>ref,y</sub>, r<sub>ref,z</sub>) corresponds to the coordinates of the atom i at its reference position and m<sub>i</sub> is the mass of atom i.</p><p>The RMSD curves of simulated trajectories of different alkali ions of Li<sup>+</sup>, Na<sup>+</sup>, and K<sup>+</sup> toward the nano-anode in the 20&nbsp;ns, are evaluated in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig4">4</a>.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-4" data-title="Figure 4"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig4" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 4</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/4" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig4_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig4" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig4_HTML.png" alt="figure 4" loading="lazy" width="685" height="539"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-4-desc"><p>The RMSD for three different anode systems. (<b>a</b>) LIBs system (<b>b</b>) SIBs system (<b>c</b>) PIBs system.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/4" data-track-dest="link:Figure4 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 4" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>It is seen that the RMSD curves for all systems exhibit regular geometric fluctuations. As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig4">4</a>, after 2 ns, the morphology of MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C systems well maintained stable until the end of the simulation time, at 20&nbsp;ns. It is worth mentioning that the anode material structure provides a short path with a large contact surface for the transfer/diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup>, K<sup>+</sup> and Li<sup>+</sup>, which leads to improved cycle stability and speed performance. For instance, Huang et al. designed and constructed 3D architectures of a few-layered Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>/NiCo<sub>2</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> as anode material for SIBs through the solvothermal method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 135" title="Huang, P. et al. Few-layered Ti3C2 MXene anchoring bimetallic selenide NiCo2Se4 nanoparticles for superior Sodium-ion batteries. Chem. Eng. J. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cej.2021.129161
                  
                 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR135" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4057">135</a></sup>. Interestingly, this cycle stability has also good agreement with experimental works. Yin’s group<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 115" title="Yin, F. et al. Flexible MoSe2/MXene films for Li/Na-ion hybrid capacitors. J. Power Sources 488, 229452 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR115" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4061">115</a></sup> engineered a flexible MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene electrode, serving as an anode for both SIBs and LIBs, to achieve a robust cycle performance. The MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene sandwich structure, observed during the insertion and extraction of Na<sup>+</sup>/Li<sup>+</sup>, demonstrates the capability to achieve high energy and power densities, reaching maximum values of 110.1&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> and 4764.7&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, as well as 84.9&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> and 3288.3&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, respectively.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6">Ion diffusion</h3><p>The mean-square displacement (MSD) is investigated to study the migration behaviour of LIBs/SIBs/PIBs toward the anode material.</p><p>The mean squared displacement (MSD) over time is employed to evaluate how target particle(s) diffuse within a system and can provide a good approximation of diffusion which is defined as:</p><div id="Equ20" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{MSD }}\left( {\text{t}} \right) \, = {\raise0.7ex\hbox{$1$} \!\mathord{\left/ {\vphantom {1 N}}\right.\kern-0pt} \!\lower0.7ex\hbox{$N$}}\sum\nolimits_{i = 1}^{N} {\left\langle {\left[ {r_{i} \left( {t_{0} + t} \right)^{2} } \right] - \left[ {r_{i} (t_{0} )} \right]^{2} } \right\rangle }$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (20)
                </div></div><p>where r<sub>i</sub> (t) describes the position of i atoms at time t, r<sub>i</sub> (t<sub>0</sub>) is the original position of i atoms, N denotes the number of atoms, and the angular bracket &lt; &gt; denotes the time average.</p><p>We plotted the MSD versus the time to ensure enough time had elapsed for the simulations. Furthermore, the MSD curves of each system indicate that the ions in the different systems have different diffusion tendencies. The highest MSD value at time t, indicating that the ions quickly diffuse and are far away from their initial positions. Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig5">5</a> illustrates the MSD curves for (a) Li<sup>+</sup>, (b) Na<sup>+</sup> (c) K<sup>+</sup> along the z-axis toward the anode material in the simulated systems. As depicted in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig5">5</a>, the MSD curve is linear, and its slope enhances with time. This finding confirms that the long-range AMIBs migrate toward the corresponding anode material structure. However, the slope of the MSD curve for Li<sup>+</sup> is more than the other ions; thus, it can be concluded that the migration of Li<sup>+</sup> is less than two other ions. This phenomenon can be attributed to the weaker diffusion of Li<sup>+</sup> than to Na<sup>+</sup>/k<sup>+</sup>. In addition, this behaviour is caused by the repulsive interactions between monovalent Li<sup>+</sup> and anode material, which is due to the small size of Li<sup>+</sup> and their higher charge density. So, in the LIBs system, the proposed anode cannot be suitable for the storage of LIBs and has no excellent cycling ability. In contrast, the Na<sup>+</sup> are allowed to migrate almost freely along the direction of the anode materials; furthermore, they prefer to coordinate into the internal space of the anode active materials. Several studies have reported on SIBs storage; for instance, Xie et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 136" title="Xie, X. et al. Porous Ti3C2TxMXene for ultrahigh-rate sodium-ion storage with long cycle life. ACS Appl. Nano Mater. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsanm.8b00045
                  
                 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR136" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4286">136</a></sup> reported the porous Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>Tx (p-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>Tx) MXene as a new electrode material for high-rate Na<sup>+</sup> storage. Their XRD findings illustrate that the porous configuration of p-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>Tx effectively minimizes the distance for electrolyte movement, promoting swift transport and diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> throughout the charging/discharging cycles. Even when subjected to increased current densities of 1 and 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the p-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>Tx electrodes consistently preserved capacities of 166&nbsp;Ma&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and 124&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Notably, even at an extremely high current density of 100&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the electrodes showcased a capacity of 24&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with an outstanding coulombic efficiency, achieving an impressive high-rate capability of 99%.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-5" data-title="Figure 5"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig5" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 5</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/5" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig5_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig5" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig5_HTML.png" alt="figure 5" loading="lazy" width="685" height="529"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-5-desc"><p>MSD patterns for investigated systems. (<b>a</b>) LIBs system (<b>b</b>) SIBs system (<b>c</b>) PIBs system.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/5" data-track-dest="link:Figure5 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 5" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Their XRD results demonstrate that the porous structure of p-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>Tx significantly reduces the distance that electrolytes to facilitate the rapid transportation and diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> during the charging/discharging cycle. At high current densities of 1 and 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the p-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>Tx electrodes consistently retained capacities of 166&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and 124&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Remarkably, even at an exceptionally high current density of 100&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the electrodes demonstrated a capacity of 24&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with a remarkable coulombic efficiency, reaching a high-rate capability of 99%.</p><p>Besides, MXenes has been reported that MXenes can be used as electrode materials for storing SIBs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhong, W. et al. MXene-derivative pompon-like Na2Ti3O7@ C anode material for advanced sodium ion batteries. Chem. Eng. J. 378, 122209 (2019)." href="#ref-CR137" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4378">137</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Sharma, M. et al. Quantum energy storage in 2D heterointerfaces. Adv. Mater. Interfaces 10(11), 2202058 (2023)." href="#ref-CR138" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4378_1">138</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 139" title="Li, C. et al. Preparation of rGO/MXene@ NiCo-P and rGO/MXene@ Fe2O3 positive and negative composite electrodes for high-performance asymmetric supercapacitors. J. Energy Storage 56, 105986 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR139" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4381">139</a></sup>. Moreover, the unique attributes of the MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@carbon-coated nanosheet can be ascribed to the exceptionally conductive functionalized MXene substrate, specifically the (Ti–O–Mo) nanorods. These nanorods contribute to a shortened Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion distance and provide abundant storage sites, enhancing overall performance. Besides, MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C acknowledged as a superior anode material, can proficiently diminish the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion barrier and reveal a greater number of active sites for Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 133" title="Liu, M. et al. Dual mechanism for sodium based energy storage. Small 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/smll.202206922
                  
                 (2023)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR133" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4396">133</a></sup>. In particular, the anchoring of 2D bimetal nanosheets on the MXene substrate offers a high specific capacity and mitigates volume expansion. Moreover, the MXene substrate serves to shorten the diffusion pathway of Na<sup>+</sup> and enhance electronic conductivity. Meanwhile, PIBs tend to adsorb onto the surface of the graphene, so they have less mobility during the charge/discharge process. Therefore, K<sup>+</sup> adsorbing by abrupt jumps on the carbon layer surface would form potassium clusters limiting graphene’s application as an anode material. However, this evidence shows that Na<sup>+</sup> are much more active than K<sup>+</sup>, so Na<sup>+</sup> diffuse much faster than K<sup>+</sup> toward the anode materials during the charging and discharging process. Since the frequency of oscillations in the MSD curves of AMIBs is low, it can be assumed that the systems during the migration of ions toward the anode material reach convergence and a stable state. Specifically, the hierarchical porous structure based on nanosheets with ultrathin 2D architecture transport path for electron and alkali ions diffusion. And also provides a larger contact area between anode and ions, which leads to improved charge transfer resistance during cycling and speed performance. Nevertheless, the fast transport of ions can be attributed to the excellent performance of the MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C structure, mainly due to the carbon coating and its surface interactions.</p><p>Based on the findings, Na<sup>+</sup> release exhibited a good tendency toward the anode materials, with a high capacity during simulation. This observation aligns well with the experimental results. As example, Tan’s research group<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 140" title="Tan, Y. et al. Carbon-coated MoSe2/MXene heterostructures as active materials for high-performance Na+ batteries. Mater. Today Commun. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.mtcomm.2022.103740
                  
                 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR140" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4420">140</a></sup> investigated a new material called MoSe<sub>2</sub>@Mo<sub>2</sub>CTX/C, which has great ionic conductivity and maintains its structural integrity during the insertion and release of sodium ions. They introduced this substance into a half-cell and examined it under rates of 0.5, 1, and 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for 2200 cycles. The obtained capacities stood at 652.2, 484.4, and 238.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, while the capacity retention values were associated about 102.5%, 103.9%, and 86.3%. Their findings represented that MoSe<sub>2</sub>@Mo<sub>2</sub>CTX/C has good potential as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries. On the other hand, Wang et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 141" title="Wang, H. et al. Sodium storage and transport properties in pyrolysis synthesized MoSe2 nanoplates for high performance sodium-ion batteries. J. Power Sources 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.02.096
                  
                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR141" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4437">141</a></sup> reported that both theoretical and experimental assessment of layered MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanoplates as the anode materials. The results illustrated well potential of MoSe<sub>2</sub> as an anode material for SIBs. They discovered that the theoretical specific capacity of bulk MoSe<sub>2</sub> can reach up to 422.28&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Additionally, their XRD findings revealed that MoSe<sub>2</sub> exhibits impressive initial discharge/charge capacities of 513 and 440&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, along with excellent cycling performance.</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec7">Computation of pair distribution functions</h4><p>The radial distribution function (RDF) generally describes the probability of finding a particle at a distance r from the reference particle<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 142" title="Yarovsky, I. Atomistic simulation of interfaces in materials: Theory and applications. Aust. J. Phys. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1071/P96118
                  
                 (1997)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR142" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4461">142</a></sup>. RDF analysis can explain the migration of AMIBs toward anode material, which provides significant insight into the accumulation of alkali ions formed around LIB/SIB/PIB systems. The radial distribution function for a pair of species ij is denoted as gij(r) and the mentioned relationship is mathematically represented by the following equation:</p><div id="Equ21" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$${\text{g}}_{{{\text{ij}}}} ({\text{r}}) = {\raise0.7ex\hbox{${n\left( r \right)}$} \!\mathord{\left/ {\vphantom {{n\left( r \right)} {4\pi r^{2} dr\rho }}}\right.\kern-0pt} \!\lower0.7ex\hbox{${4\pi r^{2} dr\rho }$}}$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (21)
                </div></div><p>The expression describes the quantity n(r), which represents the number of j ions or molecules found at a radial distance r from the location of the i ion or molecule. Here, 4πr<sup>2</sup> dr represents the volume of a shell with a thickness of dr at the radial distance r, and ρ is the bulk number density of the j molecule or ion. The results of RDF analysis for the alkali ions are illustrated in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig6">6</a>. It can be observed from this Figure RDF is zero for a short distance and is not observed any sharp peak in this region, owing to strong repulsive forces between AMIBs and anode material in the short range (&gt; 0.4&nbsp;nm). The RDF diagram shows distinct peaks in the systems containing LIBs/SIBs/PIBs; the order of their peak heights is SIBs-system &gt; PIBs-system &gt; LIBs-system. As seen in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig6">6</a>, the LIBs system’s RDF peak is weak intensity due to the weak interaction of Li<sup>+</sup> with anode materials and which appeared at about ~ 1.45&nbsp;nm. On the other hand, in the LIBs system, some Na<sup>+</sup> are trapped by Mexen, interacting with existing titanium atoms, preventing the passage of other Li<sup>+</sup> towards the anode material. The obtained results showed that the highest peak of the RDF belongs to the Na<sup>+</sup> in the SIB anode system, which appeared at about ~ 0.85. Notably, it can be ascribed to Mo–O–Ti bonds, indicating the creation of covalent bonds at the interface MXene flakes and, MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets, significantly enhancing the interaction of the two components. Moreover, the exceptional adsorption capacity of SIBs is a direct result of their profound affinity for the material’s surface, effectively impeding the migration of Na<sup>+</sup>, where the coulombic interaction between the anode materials and monovalent alkaline ions is much greater than the other ions.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-6" data-title="Figure 6"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig6" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 6</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/6" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig6_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig6" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-024-54214-6/MediaObjects/41598_2024_54214_Fig6_HTML.png" alt="figure 6" loading="lazy" width="685" height="577"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-6-desc"><p>RDFs of the three alkali ions with respect to the anode materials surface in the investigat-ed systems. (<b>a</b>) LIBs system (<b>b</b>) SIBs system (<b>c</b>) PIBs system.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6/figures/6" data-track-dest="link:Figure6 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 6" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Research groups have theorized that Na<sup>+</sup> can diffuse via low-dispersion boundary layers, which makes MXenes effective for SIB applications. This property is useful for constructing MXene-based SIB anodes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Sharma, G. et al. Calorimetric study of alkali metal ion (K+, Na+, Li+) exchange in a clay-like MXene. J. Phys. Chem. C. 121(28), 15145 (2017)." href="#ref-CR114" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4610">114</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yin, F. et al. Flexible MoSe2/MXene films for Li/Na-ion hybrid capacitors. J. Power Sources 488, 229452 (2021)." href="#ref-CR115" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4610_1">115</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yang, X. et al. Porous hollow carbon spheres decorated with molybdenum diselenide nanosheets as anodes for highly reversible lithium and sodium storage. Nanoscale 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/c5nr01909e
                  
                 (2015)." href="#ref-CR116" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4610_2">116</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Li, J. et al. Metal selenides find plenty of space in architecting advanced sodium/potassium ion batteries. Small 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/smll.202305021
                  
                 (2024)." href="#ref-CR117" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4610_3">117</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhang, Z. et al. Hierarchical MoSe2 nanosheets/reduced graphene oxide composites as anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries with enhanced electrochemical performance. ChemNanoMat 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/cnma.201500097
                  
                 (2015)." href="#ref-CR118" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4610_4">118</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhong, F. et al. Confining MoSe2 nanosheets into N-doped hollow porous carbon microspheres for fast-charged and long-life potassium-ion storage. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 13(50), 59882 (2021)." href="#ref-CR119" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4610_5">119</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 120" title="Silva, L. A. &amp; Correia, J. C. G. GEMS-Pack: A graphical user interface for the packmol program. J. Chem. Inf. Model. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.jcim.9b00740
                  
                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR120" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4613">120</a></sup>. It is worth noting that these results agree with the results of the previous sections. A close inspection of Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#Fig6">6</a> indicates that in the PIBs system, a strong peak appeared at around 1.35; it confirms that the resident time of ions on their respective sites is much longer than their spent time outside of the hopping locations site. This fact can be attributed to the radius of PIBs; thus, large ions of K<sup>+</sup> so strongly adsorbed on the active sites at the PIBs anode surface. Therefore, indicating that the time spent in the active site of anode material is significantly longer than the hopping time. In addition, the large radius of K<sup>+</sup> makes anode materials challenging during repeated K<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction. Yuan et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Yuan, Z. et al. Composites of NiSe2@C hollow nanospheres wrapped with Ti3C2Tx MXene for synergistic enhanced sodium storage. Chem. Eng. J. 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cej.2021.132394
                  
                 (2022)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4627">35</a></sup> devised a novel approach by designing highly conductive 3D hierarchical network composites, NiSe<sub>2</sub>@C@MXene, for advanced sodium ion storage. The synergistic combination of these components resulted in exceptional reversibility and long-term stability, demonstrated by a capacity of 327&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 4000 cycles.</p><p>In summary, the exceptionally conductive MXene substrate can improve electronic conductivity by anchoring nanosheets (MoSe<sub>2</sub>) chemical groups. Additionaly, the carbon layer strengthens the composite structure and further increases the hybrid nanosheets’ overall conductivity. Most importantly, the key point is achieving fast LIBs/SIBs/PIBs diffusion kinetics in the MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C interlayer. In this regard, this study emphasized that in the SIB/PIB anode systems, the presences of Na<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup> are more likely than Li<sup>+</sup> around the anode material.</p><p>We found that the presence of MXene helped in shortening the path of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion and prevented the degradation of MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets due to their large volume expansion that occurs during its interaction via the Na<sup>+</sup> and electrode. Furthermore, the morphology of the material remained unchanged after simulation, indicating that it has a certain level of stability. Finally, it is found that Na<sup>+</sup> has a more negative potential energy compared to Li<sup>+</sup> and K<sup>+</sup>. This indicates a significant interaction of Na<sup>+</sup> with the anode material surface. This phenomenon occurs due to the weaker diffusion of Li<sup>+</sup> compared to Na<sup>+</sup>/K<sup>+</sup>. The repulsive interactions between the anode material and monovalent Li<sup>+</sup> are the primary reason behind this behavior due to the small size of Li<sup>+</sup> and its higher charge density. It’s important to note that the findings validate the idea that the systematic nanostructure design of carbon-coated MoSe<sub>2</sub>-MXene has the potential to greatly improve the storage performance of AMIBs. The hierarchical anode materials demonstrated great performance in the aspect of elevated capacity and exceptional rate capability for advanced monovalent ion batteries (AMIBs), particularly in the case of SIBs. Notably, 2D highly conductive MXene serves as a suitable SIBs host<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 119" title="Zhong, F. et al. Confining MoSe2 nanosheets into N-doped hollow porous carbon microspheres for fast-charged and long-life potassium-ion storage. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 13(50), 59882 (2021)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR119" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4682">119</a></sup> and enhances reaction kinetics when coupled with transition metal oxides (TMOs) (such as MoS<sub>2</sub> and MoSe<sub>2</sub>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 104" title="Dong, Y. et al. Recent advances and promise of MXene-based nanostructures for high-performance metal ion batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 30(47), 2000706 (2020)." href="/articles/s41598-024-54214-6#ref-CR104" id="ref-link-section-d94775696e4690">104</a></sup>.</p><p>Nevertheless, the fast transport of ions can be attributed to the excellent performance of the MoSe<sub>2</sub>/MXene@C structure, mainly due to the carbon coating and its surface interactions.</p></div></div></section>
